فإن قيل : إنه لا معنى لكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة إلا كونه تعالى مباينا للعالم ، منفردا عنه ممتازا عنه وكونه تعالى كذلك ، لا يقتضي وجود أمر آخر سوى ذات الله تعالى ، فبطل قولكم إنه تعالى لو كان حاصلا في الحيز والجهة ، لكان مفتقرا إلى الغير. والذي بدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أنه لا نزاع في أن العالم مختص بالحيز والجهة ، وكونه كذلك لا معنى له إلا كون بعض الجواهر ممتازا عن البعض، منفرداً عنه وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ؟ والجواب : أما قوله : « الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجوداً في الأعيان ، فجوابه : إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أنها أشياء موجودة في الأعيان ، وبعد قيام البراهين القاطعة على صحة هذه المقدمة ، فإنه لا يبقى في صحتها شك . وأما قوله : : المراد من كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم ، أو ممتازاً عنه ، أو مباينا عنه . . فنقول : هذه الألفاظ كلها محتملة، فإن الانفراد والامتياز والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك مما لا نزاع فيه ، ولكنه لا يقتضي الجهة . والدليل عليه : أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفة لحقيقة الحيز والجهة وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة. فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى عن الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى. وإلا لزم التسلسل . وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة والحيز ، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه : أنه ههنا أو هناك . وهذا مراد الخصم من قوله : إنه تعالى مباين عن العالم ومنفرد عنه ، وممتاز عنه . إلا أنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أن هذا يقتضي كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا [ ويقتضي أن يكون الحاصل في ذلك الحيز محتاجا إلى الحيز وقوله : « الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز، فنقول : هذا ] يقتضي أن تكون الأجسام محتاجة إلى الأحياز، وهذا غير ممتنع . أما كونه تعالى محتاجا إلى شيء آخر فهو ممتنع . فظهر الفرق
If it is said: There is no meaning to His being particularized by space and direction except that He is separate (mubayin) from the world, distinct (munfarid) from it, and distinguished (mumtaz) from it; and His being so does not necessitate the existence of another thing besides God's essence. So your statement that if He were located in space and direction He would be dependent on another is invalid. And what indicates the correctness of what we mentioned is that there is no dispute that the world is particularized by space and direction, and its being so has no meaning except that some substances are distinguished from others, separate from them. And if we understand this meaning here, why is it not permissible to have the like in His being particularized by space and direction? The answer: As for his saying 'Space and direction are not existing things in external entities,' the answer is: We have demonstrated by conclusive proofs that they are things existing in external entities, and after the conclusive proofs have been established for the correctness of this premise, no doubt remains about its correctness. And as for his saying 'The meaning of His being particularized by space and direction is that He is distinct from the world, or distinguished from it, or separate from it,' we say: These expressions are all ambiguous. For 'distinction' (al-infirād), 'differentiation' (al-imtiyāz), and 'separation' (al-mubāyana) may be mentioned and intended by them difference in reality and quiddity (al-māhiyya). That is beyond dispute, but it does not entail direction. The proof of that is that the reality of God's essence is different from the reality of space and direction, and this difference and separation is not by direction. For the differentiation of God's essence from direction is not by another direction; otherwise, an infinite regress (tasalsul) would follow. And these expressions may be mentioned and intended by them differentiation in direction and space, which is that a thing is such that it can be pointed to as being 'here' or 'there.' And this is the intention of the opponent in his saying that He is separate from the world, distinct from it, and distinguished from it. However, we have demonstrated by conclusive proofs that this entails that that space is an existing thing [and entails that the thing located in that space is in need of the space. And his saying: 'Bodies are located in spaces,' we say: this] entails that bodies are in need of spaces, and this is not impossible. As for Him, exalted, being in need of something else, that is impossible. So the difference is clear.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage handles an objection and its refutation. The objector claims that saying 'God is in space or direction' merely means that God is distinct from the world, not that there is an actual spatial container. The objector argues that if the world is in space without implying a separate container, then God can also be described as 'in space' in the same sense. The author responds in two parts. First, he reasserts that space and direction are real existing entities, proven by conclusive arguments, so the objection misunderstands the nature of space. Second, he distinguishes two meanings of 'distinction', 'separation', and 'differentiation': one is conceptual difference in reality and quiddity (which does not imply spatiality), and the other is actual spatial differentiation (which does imply a location and thus dependence). The opponent intends the latter, but the author has already proven that such spatiality requires dependence. The author further explains that bodies being in space is not impossible, but God being dependent is impossible. Thus the difference between God and creatures is clear.

Key Terms
مباينة (mubāyana)
امتياز (imtiyāz)
انفراد (infirād)
حقيقة (ḥaqīqa)
ماهية (māhiyya)
تسلسل (tasalsul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: When we say God is distinct from the world, it means He is spatially separate from it.
Correction: Distinction can mean conceptual difference in essence, not spatial separation. Spatial separation implies dependence, which God is free from.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main point in responding to the objection about the meaning of 'being in space'?
A) The objection is valid and God can be in space without dependence.
B) The term 'distinction' can only mean one thing, which is spatial.
C) 'Distinction' can mean conceptual difference or spatial separation, and the opponent intends the latter, which entails dependence.
D) Space does not exist in external reality.

Key Takeaway
God's transcendence means He is not spatially distinct from the world; any spatial relationship implies need, which is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you unconsciously picture Him as being 'somewhere'—perhaps above the heavens? How does this passage's warning against spatial concepts challenge that mental image, and what will you do to align your heart with His true transcendence?
?
The author insists that any spatial relationship implies need and dependence. Reflect: in your daily life, do you sometimes treat Allah as if He is 'close' in a spatial sense, expecting Him to be physically near? How can you cultivate an awareness of His nearness through knowledge and power rather than location?
?
The infinite regress argument shows that if Allah were distinct from space by another space, it would go on forever—this highlights His absolute uniqueness. How does that uniqueness demand that you direct all your worship and attention to Him alone? What competing loyalties in your heart need to be removed to fulfill that demand?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
5 min
God's Separation Does Not Imply Need for Another
The author refutes the opponent's claim and introduces an analogy from the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the opponent's claim that God's being 'mubayin' (separate) from the world does not require another existent, and you will see the logical analogy drawn from the world's spatial properties.

Core Idea
God's separation from the world does not necessitate another existent; the same logic applies to spatial location.

In this passage, the author directly challenges the opponent's assertion that God's being 'mubayin' (separate) from the world does not necessitate any other existent. He then introduces a key analogy: the world itself is in space and direction, yet that simply means atoms are distinct from each other. Why then cannot the same apply to God? This sets the stage for a deeper debate about the meaning of spatial terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Notice the rhythm of the argument.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent implies that if God were in space and direction, He would be in need of another. Find the sentence that states this.
The opponent's view is embedded in the author's refutation.
3
Analyze the author's counter-argument
The author first declares that God's being separate does not entail another existent. Then he presents evidence from the world: the world is in space/direction, yet that merely means atoms are distinct.
Notice the rhetorical question at the end.
4
Reflect on the analogy
Consider why the author thinks the world's spatial distinctness is a valid parallel for God. What is the logical principle at work?
This analogy is central to the author's strategy.

تعالى مباينا للعالم ، منفردا عنه ممتازا عنه وكونه تعالى كذلك ، لا يقتضي وجود أمر آخر سوى ذات الله تعالى ، فبطل قولكم إنه تعالى لو كان حاصلا في الحيز والجهة ، لكان مفتقرا إلى الغير. والذي بدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أنه لا نزاع في أن العالم مختص بالحيز والجهة ، وكونه كذلك لا معنى له إلا كون بعض الجواهر ممتازا عن البعض، منفرداً عنه وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ؟ والجواب : أما قوله : « الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجوداً في الأعيان ، فجوابه : إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أنها أشياء موجودة في الأعيان ، وبعد قيام البراهين القاطعة على صحة هذه المقدمة ، فإنه لا يبقى في صحتها شك . وأما قوله : : المراد من كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم ، أو ممتازاً عنه ، أو مباينا عنه . . فنقول : هذه الألفاظ كلها محتملة، فإن الانفراد والامتياز والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك مما لا نزاع فيه ، ولكنه لا يقتضي الجهة . والدليل عليه : أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفة لحقيقة الخيز والجهة وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة. فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى عن الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى. وإلا لزم التسلسل . وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة والحيز ، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه : أنه ههنا أو هناك . وهذا مراد الخصم من قوله : إنه تعالى مباين عن العالم ومنفرد عنه ، وممتاز عنه . إلا أنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أن هذا يقتضي كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا [ ويقتضي أن يكون الحاصل في ذلك الحيز محتاجا إلى الحيز وقوله : « الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز، فنقول : هذا (١) ] يقتضي أن تكون الأجسام محتاجة إلى الأحياز، وهذا غير ممتنع . أما كونه تعالى محتاجا إلى شيء آخر فهو ممتنع . فظهر الفرق
He, exalted, is separate from the world, unique from it, distinct from it, and His being thus does not necessitate the existence of another matter besides the essence of God, exalted. So your statement is false that if He were located in space and direction, He would be in need of another. And what indicates the correctness of what we mentioned is that there is no dispute that the world is specific to space and direction, and its being so has no meaning except that some atoms are distinct from others, unique from them. And if we understand this meaning here, why is the like of it not permissible in His being, exalted, specific to space and direction? The answer: As for his saying, 'Space and direction are not existent things in external entities,' the response is that we have demonstrated with conclusive proofs that they are existent things in external entities, and after the establishment of conclusive proofs of the correctness of this premise, no doubt remains about its correctness. And as for his saying, 'What is meant by His being, exalted, specific to space and direction is His being, exalted, unique from the world, or distinct from it, or separate from it,' we say: These expressions are all ambiguous, for uniqueness, distinction, and separation may be mentioned and what is meant by them is opposition in reality and essence. That is indisputable, but it does not necessitate direction. The proof of it is that the essence of God, exalted, is opposed to the essence of space and direction, and this opposition and separation is not by direction. For the distinction of the essence of God, exalted, from direction is not by another direction, otherwise infinite regress would follow. And these expressions may be mentioned and what is meant by them is distinction in direction and space, which is a thing's being such that it is correct to point to it as 'here' or 'there.' This is what the opponent intends by his saying that He, exalted, is separate from the world, unique from it, and distinct from it. Except that we have demonstrated with conclusive proofs that this necessitates that that space is an existing thing and necessitates that the one located in that space is in need of the space. And his saying, 'Bodies are located in spaces,' we say: This necessitates that bodies are in need of spaces, and this is not impossible. But that He, exalted, is in need of something else is impossible. So the difference is clear.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. The author begins by quoting an opponent's claim: that God's being 'mubayin' (separate) from the world does not imply a need for another existent, and thus the argument that if God were in space He would need something else is false. The author first clarifies that the world's being in space simply means that atoms are distinct from each other, and asks why the same could not apply to God. Then he addresses two specific points from the opponent. First, the opponent claims space and direction are not real things; the author asserts they have already proven they are real with conclusive proofs, so no doubt remains. Second, the opponent argues that what is meant by God's being in space is merely His distinctness from the world. The author responds by noting that terms like 'infirad' (uniqueness), 'imtiyaz' (distinction), and 'mubayana' (separation) are ambiguous. They can mean essential difference (which does not entail direction) or spatial distinction (which does). The opponent intends the latter. The author proves that essential difference does not require direction because God's essence is different from the reality of space itself, and that difference is not by a direction (otherwise infinite regress). However, spatial distinction would require an existing space and make the occupant in need of that space. Bodies need spaces — that is not impossible — but God's needing something else is impossible. Thus the difference between bodies and God is clear.

Key Terms
مباينة (mubayana, separation)
انفراد (infirad, uniqueness)
امتياز (imtiyaz, distinction)
حيز (hayyiz, space)
جهة (jiha, direction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God is described as 'mubayin' (separate), He must be in need of a space to be separate from, or that separation implies another entity.
Correction: The author clarifies that God's being separate from the world does not require any other existent; separation can be an attribute of His essence without entailment of a spatial container.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the author use to support his argument that God's being in space and direction would not imply need?
A) The world's atoms are distinct from each other in space
B) Conclusive proofs from earlier
C) The opponent's own admission
D) The impossibility of infinite regress

Key Takeaway
The author uses the world's spatial distinctness as an analogy to argue that God's being in space would not imply need for another existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unconsciously imagined God as being 'far away' in a spatial sense, and what does this lesson teach you about the danger of that assumption? Today, face one private thought where you limited God to a location or distance, and repent from it.
?
The author uses the world's own structure as evidence for God. Look at your own life: in what area have you accepted a false 'necessity' about God because of how you see the world? Write down one worldly assumption you hold about God and ask yourself if it is truly necessary.
?
If God's separation from the world does not imply need for another, then your own separation from Allah due to sin does not require a human mediator to bring you back—only His mercy. Will you turn to Him directly today and abandon any false intermediary you have relied upon?
